==PAGE:105==
Discussion 8
The output of this project is a prototype platform for recording and sharing
driver perspective video between haulers and insurance companies through a web
application. During the course of the project, several aspects have been left open
and require discussion.
8.1
Risk Reﬂections
At project initiation, a risk analysis was conducted to more eﬀectively handle
threats. In general, the overall mitigation strategies as a result of the analysis proved
useful. This can especially be said in regards to transferring the legal aspects. The
analysis outlined a limited portion of the laws to consider; however, for a ﬁnal
product, the analysis is acknowledged insuﬃcient.
In regards to the law, every
country has its own speciﬁc set of rules which must be identiﬁed and respected.
Another correctly identiﬁed risk was communication limitations. Although multiple
attempts were made to contact both haulers, drivers, and insurance companies, it
was mainly the AUGIT network that provided the ’correct’ users involved in this
project. In this regard, the strategy cannot be said to be followed to perfection.
When it came to testing, and no haulers had time, the authors sought aid from
their network. This provided some qualiﬁed test subjects, but later it was found
that the AUGIT network included TEC, which is a driving school for truck drivers.
When contacted, a test session could not be conducted within the time remaining
in the project. This was otherwise a test scenario that could have been beneﬁcial if
organized in due time.
Further learnings were made to manage participants for tests as the ﬁrst four
intended subjects for the Driver Accept Experiment canceled their appointments.
These appointments were made as a casual agreement stating that the authors
should return at the beginning of a speciﬁed week and then schedule for precise
date and time. When the time came for the ﬁnal scheduling, the participants had
all made other arrangements. Understandably, this project is neither the ﬁrst, the
second, or maybe even the ﬁfth priority of the drivers, which could be the result
of the cancellations. It could also be that since no date and time were speciﬁed in
early agreements, only a week, then the participants did not note down that they
93
==PAGE:106==
Master Thesis
8. Discussion
had signed up for the experiment. From this, it was learned that when making
arrangements, it is advantageous to be well in advance with the details. Another
potential solution could have been to gain the hauler contact information from these
drivers and schedule for tests through him.
During the project, more risks came to be than initially considered. These were
favorably risks that could be managed using the existing contingency plans made at
project initiation, i.e., no additional time had to be used to identify new management
methods as existing strategies could be transferred to ﬁt the new threats.
An
example of this is that prior to receiving the AR glasses from AUGIT, the needed
amount of USB ports was not considered. As it turned out, when the glasses arrived,
they required more ports than were originally available. For this, the contingency for
equipment availability could have been utilized; however, an alternative computer
was found.
The general risk analysis can be said to be reasonably correct based upon the
experiences during the project.
Some identiﬁed risks, such as AUGIT software
complexity and equipment availability, never came to be a threat while new arose due
to the nature of an agile process. In hindsight, for future learnings, own equipment
failure should also be included as this was a near-miss in the project. Luckily with
the sharing mechanisms available today, such as GitHub, this had no signiﬁcant
consequences.
Risks are often divided into two segments to outline that risks can also imply a
positive outcome. The negative, which has just been examined, are called threats,
and the positive are called opportunities. An opportunity that arose during the
project was the multiple domains uncovered where the video could also beneﬁt
drivers and haulers.
8.2
Video Application Domains
During the project, three application areas were found where video recorded from
the driver’s perspective could be of use: Education, Research and Insurance cases.
One was quickly discarded, two were carried until the end of the analysis where one
was followed through to the development and test of the prototype platform.
8.2.1
Education
Video from the driver’s perspective is ideal in education where the use could beneﬁt
both new and experienced drivers. If excluding the functionality of the AUGIT
glasses (to ’see-through’ the solid surfaces of the truck), then truck drivers cannot
act in a truck as they normally would in a car by cause of sight limitations. This is
evident, and as a consequence, they have to be careful when consulting their mirrors
94
==PAGE:107==
8. Discussion
DTU
for proper orientation. As a ﬁrst step, the video can be used to actively engage driver
students in their behavior and highlight where changes can be made for safer road
travels. As a second step, the video can be used for license oﬃcials to evaluate
more accurately if all mirrors have been properly consulted, i.e., are the skills of the
driver becoming for acquiring a license. That said, the video is not enough. Imagine
yourself driving and checking your back rear mirror. Do you move your head all
the way and look directly at the mirror or do you glimpse with a small rotation?
In most cases, a person glimpses towards the mirror making it hard to judge if a
mirror was consulted based solely on the video, as such the additional feature of
eye-tracking is needed for the video to have its desired eﬀect within education.
By cause of the current prototype not supporting eye-tracking, this perspective was
closed as a project pursuit after the initial inspection. Being as it may, a notion
of hardware advancements within this regard is made for future iterations of the
product as the analysis has shown the potential for a positive eﬀect on road safety.
Also, eye-tracking was proposed as a feature desirable for research purposes.
8.2.2
Research
The limits for the video within the research domain are hard to deﬁne. Existing
research could beneﬁt from the ﬁrst-person video, and with it, new opportunities
arise. Once again, eye-tracking would beneﬁt the general research application, but
there are areas where the current video is applicable. E.g., from the raw video, it
can be observed if drivers tend to look more away from the road if a co-driver is
present. It can be seen if a VRU is in the driver’s ﬁeld of view. It can be seen what
the weather conditions are and so on.
In addition, although not investigated in detail, the implementation of external
video analysis software can tag the videos with various attributes. This can then be
used as search criteria, privacy mechanisms, or the possibility of using the videos in
studies with larger sample size. With this, the criticism of the DBQ accuracy can
be resolved as the driver’s self-image, and memory can be compared with that of
reality.
Returning to the addition of eye-tracking, then studies can be made more eﬃcient
in relation to determine the eﬀect of new road designs or campaigns. Eye-tracking
can show if the drivers notice the stop signs, the speed limit, the blind spots. It
can also be used to study when focus decreases and the eﬀect. As for now, the sky
is the limit, and there is evident potential for the ﬁrst-person video to be of use
within research. It is noted that the video can be used as-is, and it can be further
advanced to support eye-tracking for optimal usage.
95
==PAGE:108==
Master Thesis
8. Discussion
8.2.3
Insurance
As a ﬁnalist among the three application domains is insurance companies where the
videos can be used to protect drivers against false insurance accusations. In this
case, the raw video is suﬃcient and directly beneﬁts the customer of the glasses,
namely the hauler, within the limitation that the driver has observed the incident.
Not saying that research and education do not beneﬁt the hauler, they do; however,
it is done with high transparency meaning that the hauler or driver might never
feel the diﬀerence as results tend to be small adjustments over time to improve the
overall situation.
As such, also inﬂuenced by the desire from CODAN, the insurance perspective was
chosen to follow through in relation to validating the potential for the video as a
business case. In hindsight, from a strategic point of view, this can also be said to
pave the way for the remaining perspectives. Though with a small diﬀerence, the
ﬁrst questionnaire and the driver accept experiment both showed that more drivers
were willing to provide video for their employer than for research. It is speculated
that it can be too invasive to provide personal information to strangers when the
eﬀect is unknown. As is with speculations, this should be further validated before
making any conclusions; however, with the insurance perspective as a ﬁrst target,
this is transferred to future stages.
It is inconclusive which of the perspectives will beneﬁt the costumers the
most.
While research would be optimal in general aspects such as road design
improvements, education will be beneﬁcial in creating more skilled drivers, and
insurance can aid drivers if guilt is wrongfully placed. The eﬀect of each perspective
is left for future evaluations, but as argued, the insurance perspective is considered
a proper starting point in realizing the service.
8.3
Data
During the legal investigation, a series of questions was proposed to ask oneself when
dealing with personal data. After the analysis, these can now be answered.
Do you process personal information? Yes, the deﬁnition of processing has
been established, and as a video is stored, the platform does process personal
information.
What personal information are you treating? The information will mostly
be related to what can be seen in the video. This includes personal aspects,
such as race and gender. If considering the case where the platform is expanded
for research, then additional information from the tachograph will complement
the video.
This being age and nationality.
The remaining information is
related to the trip, not the person.
96
==PAGE:109==
8. Discussion
DTU
Why are you processing your personal information? As a general objective,
to aid drivers and haulers. If only considering the main perspective, then to aid
drivers and haulers during insurance cases. If taking in research and education
as well, the answer is not as simple. Then processing is related to further the
road design for the beneﬁt of drivers and other road users; it is related to
improving driving behavior; it is related to improving driving skills.
It is
related to every aspect that can be improved for drivers and others to co-exist
on the roads.
How do you process the personal information? As a minimum case,
the
information is recorded, stored, organized, and made available. Furthermore,
future implementations to beneﬁt education and research could provide the
notion of retrieval, adaption, and alteration.
Where do you process personal information? This
question can
only be
answered with certainty within the Danish borders.
The information is
recorded in the truck, then stored on servers from which the users can access
the data through a web application. When the video is recorded outside of
Denmark, there are several possibilities to consider. Some countries are strict
in regards to video, and some are not. In some countries, it is not allowed to
ﬁlm at all, in some countries the video cannot leave the borders, and for others,
the video can be stored just as if it was recorded in Denmark. These aspects
are important to investigate in detail when developing the ﬁnal product.
How long do you process the personal information? As there is no limit to
an insurance claim, then no limit can be set on storing the video. This is
also beneﬁcial for research, i.e., the more data, the better the predictions and
output.
After the analysis, one answer is still lacking in detail, and that is where the data is
processed. The diﬀerent laws need to be established so that a solution can be found.
This is likely to be a solution of multiple individual solutions, e.g., in countries where
the data cannot leave the boarders servers can be put in place, in countries where
they have similar laws but are less strict agreements can be made for the data to
be transferred, and in countries where no such law exists the data can be stored as
it was recorded in Denmark. The puzzle is to categorize the diﬀerent countries and
ﬁnd the proper solution. As a ﬁrst step in the product release, it could also be that
the recording automatically turns oﬀwhen crossing the border so that video is only
recorded in Denmark.
8.4
Design
During the analysis, it was explained that the end product and the prototype were
kept separate. This was done to more quickly validate with users as the ’behind the
scene’ development did not have to reﬂect that of the product. The choice proved to
97
==PAGE:110==
Master Thesis
8. Discussion
be correct in regards to this project where a meeting with the product owner could
not happen before a month into the process. Moreover, as gently touched upon in the
analysis, the project took a turn from being an extension to the insurance companies
existing software to being a full-scale online platform for video and corresponding
data. Although many resources went into the investigation of the extension, actual
development was not a major component. Therefore, the swift in direction was not
hard to do, and most research could still be transferred into the new design.
As the project progressed, so did the needs for testing, and a second part of the
system was developed as a prototype. At ﬁrst, these were intended as two separate
parts used to test diﬀerent aspects. However, the link between the two prototypes
was an interesting subject where additional security measures could be investigated,
and as such, they were combined.
In terms, this provided a more realistic test
scenario as the participants in the Driver Accept experiment could see the video
they recorded on the actual web-page. As a result, a more comprehensive mental
model of the ﬁnal solution could be developed.
Throughout the report, the term nudging has come up multiple times. During the
analysis, it was decided to include several nudging strategies though mostly minded
towards the platform as a research remedy. If the platform is not made available
for research, then some of the proposed nudgings are unnecessary as they seek to
inﬂuence the haulers in keeping the video on the platform for as long as possible,
preferably for good. If the platform is solely an insurance tool, then only videos
that are of use in a case are needed, including the nudging to make drivers record
the video.
Figure 8.1:
Recommended nudges positioned along the transparency and reﬂective-
automatic axes.
98
==PAGE:111==
8. Discussion
DTU
Figure 8.1 illustrates the proposed nudges positioned relative to their category. To
summarize the categories:
• Reﬂective-Transparent: Prompting of reﬂective choice
• Automatic-Transparent: Inﬂuence behavior
• Reﬂective-Non transparent: Manipulate choice
• Automatic-Non transparent: Manipulate behavior
As can be observed in the ﬁgure, most strategies utilized are categorized as ’prompt
for reﬂection’. Through this type of nudging, it is the intention that the haulers will
treat the data with care and make no hasted or automated actions. Though out
of scope for this project, it would be ideal for testing further if the strategies are
correctly identiﬁed or if others are more suitable.
8.5
Product Design
While not being a goal of this project, the analysis and the tests conducted with the
second prototype provided some design aspects to consider when maturing the AR
glasses. As a measure for maturing and expanding the business case, eye-tracking
can be useful. However, before that is considered a deep ﬂaw in the current hardware
must be corrected. The Driver Accept Experiment showed a most criticized short-
coming in the glasses in relation to the platform: the camera ﬁeld of view. The
camera only features an 82-degree horizontal and a 52-degree vertical ﬁeld of view,
where the human has a 180-degree horizontal and a 150-degree vertical ﬁeld of view
[114]. The limited view puts an unwanted constraint on the platform. The intent
was for the platform to contain a 1:1 perspective of what the driver can see but
the current glasses are only able to provide less of half the view. Furthermore, for
proper use, the glasses should include 6 degrees-of-freedom head tracking instead of
the currently implemented 3 degrees to account for diﬀerent heights and shapes of
the drivers.
An additional mechanism to advance the glasses would be to incorporate GNSS as
this is desired by both perspectives of hauler and research. However, as stated by
Kim Sand Andersen, most haulers today are looking for trucks with GNSS included
as their customers often want to know the whereabouts of their delivery. As such,
it can be the case that the additional GNSS in the glasses would be redundant as
the data is already in the truck, but then again, not all trucks come with tracking
devices. This is a trade-oﬀthat would have to be evaluated at later stages. It could
also be the case that AUGIT develops two versions of the system, one that includes
a tracking device in the glasses and one that utilizes an existing device in the truck.
Most problematic about glasses in this project was how to wear them. The current
design does not support all head shapes resulting in the glasses sliding down slowly
99
==PAGE:112==
Master Thesis
8. Discussion
for some. In an extreme scenario, this could be the cause of an accident as the
glasses would fall covering the eyes of the driver. Even in the mildest format, this
presents a barrier - when the glasses do not ﬁt properly, the driver will not wear
them by cause of irritation. The ill ﬁt of the glasses also proposes the challenge of
the video not reﬂecting precisely what is in the driver’s ﬁeld of view by cause of a
small rotation. If the camera is not conﬁgured to the driver’s ﬁeld of view, then
once again, the video is not guaranteed useful. This is a problem that could be
transferred to AUGIT in general.
As part of the start-up kick of in AUGIT, two of the team members produced a
report where they hypothesize diﬀerent design solutions towards the ﬁnal product.
In the report, it is inconclusive if the glasses should be wired or wireless based
on their ﬁndings. It was found during this project that when working with video
and personal data in general, the principle of minimization is essential. The aspect
of wired glasses would support this principle as the driver cannot leave the truck
with the glasses on; hence, the recording will only happen while driving.
This
also removes the other problems related to battery-driven technology in terms of
weight and availability. If it is the case that later tests show that wireless is the
way to proceed, then automatic measures to turn of recording when leaving the
truck is recommended. This again provides additional barriers to overcome as the
video should then be activated again when driving. It can be speculated that when
the drivers wear the glasses while leaving the truck, they would forget to activate
the recording once behind the wheel again. Concerning minimizing eﬀort for the
driver it would be optimal for the recording to begin when the truck is in motion
automatically, however, then it becomes an automated system which is the deﬁnition
of TV surveillance, making it illegal to ﬁlm on public roads. A strategy to overcome
this problem could be for the glasses to display a subtle message telling the driver
that the recording is not activated, thereby giving him a choice to do so.
Other design reﬂections not related to hardware have also been made. The AR
possibilities are more than that of mitigating blind spots. The start-up has shown
through their investigations that drivers are mentally more capable if not having
to consult various monitors and mirrors. In this regard, one screen that can be
replaced by the glasses is the navigation device. In a similar manner to Google
Maps, augmented reality allows for the directions to be directly paved onto the
road, thereby expanding AUGIT’s intend and adding the navigation device to the
list of redundant monitors in the vehicle.
Furthermore, smart features, such as
parking assistance, traﬃc alerts, and road warnings, could be implemented. While
beyond the project scope, both hardware and software design advancements to the
product are considered valuable learnings for the start-up.
100
==PAGE:113==
8. Discussion
DTU
8.6
Results
This project can be seen to have three overall testings or validations. First, the desire
for the platform was validated through interviews with users, then again through
usability tests complemented with interviews, and the ﬁnal validation was concerned
with drivers being willing to act as a data subject. If isolating the numbers not
considering the statistical impact, then all tests concluded with a positive outcome.
However, the validity of the outcome can be questioned.
The desire for the platform was in the spirit of validating a business case as
a start-up conducted through interviews.
Here 2/2 haulers and 5/5 insurance
representatives thought positively towards the platform. With 100% of the consulted
potential customers supporting the product, it should be considered a valid business
case. However, six people from three companies cannot be concluded to represent
the entire customer base. Throughout the project, several other companies were
contacted who either never replied or replied that they did not have the resources to
participate in the project at the time. Both could be a response of no interest in such
product, or it could be that the companies could not spare the workforce, this cannot
be known. As such, no ﬁnite validation from the general insurance perspective can
be made; however, the product is considered validated within CODAN. This was
supported by the usability test with the actual end-users of the system. From the
hauler perspective, no further validation with end-users could be made than the
initial interviews. However, usability tests were conducted with other participants
in order to eliminate immediate usability problems.
The ﬁnal validation of the
interface and product should be conducted with end-users as this provides more
accurate design aspects for a successful product.
The second phase, to validate drivers as the data subject, also had its participant
limitations, but a signiﬁcance was found, and the Herning observation was validated.
The observation being that drivers with knowledge of the system are more prone to
accept being the data subject. The experiment was a later addition to the project
as it was found necessary to validate that data would be available for the platform.
At best, this experiment can be seen as a pilot run that has provided an allusion to
that there is potential for drivers to act as data subjects. However, further testing
is needed.
The experiment was conducted by the cause of the belief that 20+
drivers could be found. In hindsight, with limited time to recruit and conduct the
experiment, this could have been foreseen as too optimistic. For future references,
it is noted that time must be considered carefully when creating experiments.
A general limitation during the project has been the recruitment of participants.
Returning to the risk analysis, this was expected to be a challenge, a challenge that
has provided some valuable learnings. A network, even that of a company, cannot
be considered as having a project’s best interests in mind and ’fall to the rescue’
101
==PAGE:114==
Master Thesis
8. Discussion
when needed. The planning in this project has relied heavily on this belief, which
instead should have been based upon the situation as is.
8.7
Recommendation
During the unfolding of this report, several recommendations have been made.
The ones concerning the AR glasses have already been established in the design
discussion, whereas this section will present only recommendations related to the
new service and the platform.
To acquire consent from the data subject is a legal necessity, and as such one should
be constructed with great care. This report has listed the minimal information that
should be given to the data subject. However, it is recommended by the director of
SikkerhedsBranchen to have a professional overlook the ﬁnal draft.
Furthermore, the law states that "Personal data shall be adequate, relevant and
limited to what is necessary in relation to the purposes for which they are processed
(‘data minimisation’);"[115]. In regards to an insurance case, the driver ID is nice
to have but far from need to have and it can be discussed if this crosses the line
of data minimization. However, the choice to include driver IDs is also based upon
another aspect of the law - that the driver has the right to have all personal data
removed from the platform. In some cases, this could be performed by running
facial recognition software, but the driver’s face is not likely to be in the video
unless caught in a mirror.
Then some could argue that the truck could be the
identiﬁer. The counterargument is that truck drivers are often behind the wheels
of several trucks in their lifetime, making this option a pain for the controller in
regards to ﬁnding the correct videos to delete. Also, manual identiﬁcation of drivers
could result in videos being overlooked.
As such, though in conﬂict with data
minimization, driver IDs are included with respect to the drivers in order to protect
their rights.
Another aspect currently in conﬂict with data minimization is how the video is
shared. As part of the MVP it was chosen to include the entire video; however,
for the actual implementation, this should be reconsidered. The user story map
presents a possible solution where the insurance company is only able to see a 20
minutes version of the video cropped around the provided incident time.
The current implementation of the platform contains a page for insurance agents
where they can locate videos if a hauler has granted access. It further contains a
page for haulers where they can locate all videos related to their business. The
second questionnaire showed that drivers want access as well. At ﬁrst, this was
considered a breach in data minimization by allowing more people access to the
videos. However, it is evident that a driver should have access to his data, and a
102
==PAGE:115==
8. Discussion
DTU
page for drivers should be created with the functionality of watching and deleting
their videos.
While currently being an insurance tool, the advancements to be made in order for
it to duplicate as a research remedy is not far away. Research beneﬁts from data,
and the more, the better. To protect privacy, the current implementation allows for
haulers to delete videos. However, if there is only a 5 minutes privacy concern in
a 4-hour video, then the whole video does not have to be deleted. Therefore, it is
recommended to add a feature where the hauler and the driver can alter the video
by blurring or removing segments instead of removing the entire video.
103
==PAGE:116==
==PAGE:117==
Conclusion 9
This project was initiated on a request from AUGIT Solutions to validate the
hypothesized business case of utilizing data in the form of video recorded from
the drivers perspective to aid haulers and drivers.
As a general scope, this is
rather broad, and several domains were found interesting for business pursuit.
However, one was chosen for more in-depth investigation, and the following goal
was established: to develop a high-ﬁdelity prototype for sharing the AUGIT video
with supplemental data in order to validate the main objective.
Main Objective
Is there a desire for such tool to be realized for
insurance agents and haulers, respectively?
Based on interviews, the insurance tool was developed as an online web application
from where the users could access the video with complementary data. This provides
easy access for multiple companies and at the same time, opens up for later use of
the video within the ﬁeld of research or potentially education.
Throughout the lifespan of the project, two overarching validations have been
performed.
The main aspect was to validate the desire for the service.
This
was obtained through user-centered development and subsequent usability tests
complemented with interviews. The second aspect was to validate that drivers would
record video for the platform, i.e., be the data subject. This was obtained through
an experiment simulating a real-life scenario, and an additional questionnaire shared
on social media to get more coverage.
This report has sought to provide recommendations towards a ﬁnal product
regarding an insurance tool based upon learnings through user interactions. The
platform is considered validated through the project customer being the insurance
company CODAN, where 4/4 claims agents stated that they would use the
application after completing a usability session. If the validation can be transferred
to a larger market segment is unknown. During the initial investigation, 2/2 haulers
stated their desire for the platform, but later validations were not conducted by the
cause of recruitment shortage.
105
==PAGE:118==
Master Thesis
9. Conclusion
The Driver Accept Experiment showed that providing drivers with knowledge about
the video content can add to the acceptance of being a data subject. Based on the
experiment results, where 6/6 participants would share their data with the employer
and insurance company, this aspect is also validated, however, based on the low
amount of participants the result is not considered conclusive. The experiment result
was supported by the questionnaire, where the same question led to a conﬁrmation
from 29 additional participants. In addition, the results were less clear in regards to
having the video used for research where only 4/6 participants currently accepted
being a data subject.

==PAGE:133==
Thesis Description B
The following two pages contain the thesis description used to initiate the project.
The project does fulﬁll the initial goal to develop and test a secure platform for
video sharing between AUGIT and insurance companies. However, as the scope
was expanded during the course of the project, the description does not fully cover
the extend of the conducted investigation (using the data for research was disclosed
in-project).
121
==PAGE:134==
Master thesis 
30 ECTS 
 
Start: 28/1-19 
Slut: 
28/6-19 
 
 
Students 
Emil Bejstrup Otterstrøm
Tanja Lind Hansen 
s131917@student.dtu.dk
s173341@student.dtu.dk  
M.Sc. Computer Science
M.Sc. Digital Media Engineering 
 
Supervisors 
Christian Damsgaard Jensen
Per Bækgaard 
cdje@dtu.dk 
pgba@dtu.dk  
Associate Professor, DTU
Associate Professor, DTU 
 
 
Titel​: 
Design af Platform til Deling af Video fra Chaufførens 
Perspektiv som Værktøj til Afklaring af Skyld i 
Forsikringssammenhæng 
- Validering af forretningsidé 
 
Title​:  
Platform Design for Sharing Novel Driver Perspective Video as 
a Remedy in Fault Claims 
- Validating the business case 
 
Context​: 
AUGIT is a startup at DTU currently working to eliminate blind spots in Heavy Goods 
Vehicles (HGV) using augmented reality (AR). The system of AR glasses and external 
camera feed enables the truck driver to ‘see through’ the chassis of his truck.  
 
Goal​: 
Remedy situation regarding question of guilt in HGV insurance cases with the AUGIT data. 
 
In order to develop a system for sharing HGV data, research in the problem domain will be 
conducted to identify the different pains from stakeholders. This includes talking to 
stakeholders such as insurance companies to scope what data is currently accessible, what 
could be of interest and how AR footage​ ​from blind spots can affect insurance claims. 
==PAGE:135==
Furthermore, the effect on the new AUGIT business case will be assessed in regards to the 
reaction from the provider of the footage and the person in question in the insurance claim 
cases, namely the driver. Moreover, based on GDPR, proper protection must be 
implemented to ensure no ethical and law violations. In relation, the project will analyze 
encryption schemes with focus on privacy implementation.  
 
Expected outcome 
A prototype interface for insurance companies to gain access to ideal HGV data for 
insurance claims including implementation of privacy protection of the data with access 
rights.  
==PAGE:136==
==PAGE:137==
Project Risks C
This appendix contains the risks identiﬁed throughout the project. The risks were
regularly revisited once a week.
C.1
Initial Risk Index
1. Communication limitations with stakeholders
a) insurance, b) hauler, c) drivers, d) AUGIT, e) researchers
2. Bias from data subject (driver)
3. Legal limitations
4. Equipment damages
5. Equipment availability
6. Unknown complexity of provided software
7. Skills in development environment
C.2
Final Risk Index
1. Communication limitations with stakeholders
a) insurance, b) hauler, c) drivers
The problem with communication with insurance can be divided in two. First,
the insurance representative could not meet within the ﬁrst month so all
communication were written which led to a misunderstanding and the project
took a turn.
Second, additional insurance companies were contacted where
those who replied did not have time and remaining never answered.
The problem with communication with haulers and drivers was the lack of
communication. No hauler had signed up for the project prior to initiation
and only two could be found within the time of the project. Several companies
have been contacted through their number found online but it is unknown who
received the message.
2. Bias from data subject (driver)
Not considered a threat at the beginning as AUGIT had previously validated this
through interview, however, conﬂicting results were found at project initiation
which had to be resolved.
125
==PAGE:138==
Master Thesis
C. Project Risks
3. Legal limitations
Minor limitations but all identiﬁed as gray areas meaning that they have not
been to court, so professionals cannot say if it is okay or not. As such, they
are considered okay, but contingencies must be made if that changes.
4. Equipment damages
This was initially thought as equipment provided from AUGIT which was no
problem in the project. Instead our own equipment threatened to break
5. Unknown complexity of software
Share GPS guide was setup to provide Google Earth with NMEA data.
This had to be modiﬁed to deliver the data to the recording system instead.
Furthermore was the Unity SDK was time consuming to work with, as it did
not have any documentation except a few examples.
6. Skills in development environment
As expected, development took longer than estimated by cause of minor
problems.
7. Hardware limitation, not enough ports in computer
The glasses from AUGIT they required 2 USB ports and the mobile phone
required one more. As such 3 ports were needed. The PC used initially had a
broken port and could not handle the set-up. In the ﬁrst laptop the ports were
placed too far apart for the wire to reach. The second laptop could handle the
setup but threatened to go black several times. (However, it did not happen)
8. Access to stakeholders
The participants for the usability tests were stationed in Aarhus (more than
340km away)
9. Participant limitations
’Correct’ users could not be recruited for hauler usability and driver accept,
as such substitutes were used to provide an indication, however, the tests will
have to be conducted at later stages with actual users.

Interview: Herning E
The interviews in Herning were conducted immediate after participants had tried
the AUGIT prototype. As such, the notes were written in a notebook. Images of
the note sheet from each of the 12 interviews are presented in the following. Figure
E.1 presents the prepared questions. The length of the interview depended on the
situation, as such not all participants were asked the same questions. However, all
were asked (question 7) who they would share the video with. The interviews were
in Danish, the main take away was that no participants said no to sharing the video
with either Employer, Insurance or Research, however, some said maybe.

Questions prepared for Herning interview.

==PAGE:146==
 
Spørgeskema 
Questionnaire 
 
 
Nedenstående (10)  spørgsmål bruges til at undersøge ansattes forhold til brugen af data der indsamles gennem en arbejdsdag. 
Besvarelsen er anonym og vil indgå i en samlet analyse til et kandidatspeciale ved Danmarks Tekniske Universitet. Nogle 
spørgsmål tager udgangspunkt i at du er chauffør. Hvis dette ikke er tilfældet besvares spørgsmålet blot ud fra din egen 
profession.  
The following (10) questions are used to investigate employee relationships with the use of data collected over a working day. 
The answer is anonymous and will be included in a comprehensive analysis for a Master's thesis at the Technical University of 
Denmark. Some questions are based on the fact that you are a driver. If this is not the case, the question is simply answered from 
your own profession.

Questionnaire #1: Results G
Figure G.1 presents the comments provided by the participants to the question:
"What signiﬁcance do you think it will have for drivers if there is video surveillance
in the cab?". The answers have been divided according to tone, i.e. if the answer
is positive towards the additional ’surveillance’ or not.
As the interpretation is
subjective the reader must not think of this as a conclusive division.
Figure G.1:
Comments on what participants think the eﬀect of video surveillance in
truck cabin will be. 34 out of 48 participants answered the question, and the comments
are categorized into three categories of tone: 9 Negative, 3 Neutral and 19 Positive toned
comment.
All answers from the questionnaires have been gathered in a spreadsheet for
overview. The columns marked in a shaded red color are female answers and the
remaining are from males.

==PAGE:157==
Interview: Legal Aspects H
H.1
SikkerhedsBranchen
In order to better understand the laws concerning the platform, an interview with the
Director of SikkerhedsBranchen Kasper Skov Mikkelsen was arranged. The interview
was in Danish, as such a summary is provided: If the platform is developed to be
used in a scientiﬁc matter, then most laws of GPDR is annulled. There is still ethics
to consider in relation to the data subject. It was learned that the video cannot be
automated as it then would fall under the laws of TV Surveillance which states that
ﬁlming in public space is illegal. In normal circumstances people should be blurred,
however, if the footage is only available in a closed forum this is not necessary. In
conclusion, if the rights of the data subject are respected, the platform is developed
with transparency and data minimization is considered then the platform is legal.
H.2
GPDR 2.0
During the course of the project, the union for engineers had a lecture in relation to
GDPR which was attended. The notes from the lecture is included in this appendix,
though in Danish. The general takeaway was that encryption tags a potential breach
as low risk. Subsequent to the notes are the lecture slides.
145
==PAGE:158==
15/03/2019 
SikkerhedsBranchen ​v. Kasper Skov Mikkelsen 
Forklaring af brille, video og platform er givet 
 
Overordnet er vi interesseret i hvad der skal til for at sådan en platform er lovlig. Det 
handler jo om filmen i offentlig rum og GDPR kan være svær at tyde på nogle punkter. 
●
Først så skal vi i hvert fald have afklaret om I ligger inden for tv overvågning for så 
kommer der jo ekstra regler i spil og så tror jeg ikke vi kan forsvare at det er lovligt 
det I gerne vil. Hvis optagelsen er automatisk så vil i falde ind under tv overvågning. 
(Der tages beslutning om at brillen ikke må være automatisk) Det er en meget lille 
aktion der skal til. Så længe chaufføren gør noget aktiv for at starte videoen, så er det 
ikke længere tv overvågning. Hvis han trykker på en knap eller laver en bevægelse. 
 
Hvis den bevægelse er at tage brillerne på, gælder det så? 
●
Ja, det er en aktiv handling for at starte optagelsen. I skal bare være opmærksom på 
at det stopper igen, sådan så at når han næste gang tager brillen på så er det ikke 
allerede i gang, for så er det automatisk i det tilfælde.  
●
Så længe i bruger paragrafferne til at drage konklusioner, så kan I ikke blive fældet 
da det er jeres opfattelse af det. Det kan godt være at I bliver bedt om at ændre 
noget fordi andre mener I har tolket forkert, men hvis I laver fortolkninger, så har I det 
rene på jeres side. I det her tilfælde ville jeg sige “Vi har ud fra §1 stk 2 afledt at det 
ikke er omfattet af tv overvågning” 
 
Hvordan forholder det sig i forhold til GDPR? 
●
Hvis I hører under forskning, så slipper i meget billigt. Rigtig mange af GDPR 
paragrafferne er nemlig annulleret hvis dataen bruges inden for forskning. 
●
I har også en fordel ved at I gerne vil bruge dataen til berigtning. Der findes jo sager 
hvor f.eks. G4S har fået lov til at opbevare video fra deres BWC fordi det skal 
beskytte de ansatte.  
●
Ifølge §6 stk 1 så kan I forsvare jeres video hvis der er en legitim grund. Undgå trafik 
drab eller uheld er et meget godt forsøg på en legitim grund. Men som så meget 
andet, så er det ikke noget der har været for retten og derfor ved man ikke så meget 
om det. 
●
Generelt er der mange gråzoner lige netop fordi at ingen sager har været for retten.  
●
Der står i GDPR at personer ikke må kunne identificeres på baggrund af dataen. Når 
man taler om video, så ser man jo normalt at det gøres ved sløring. Jeg vil dog sige 
at I godt kan argumenterer for at det ikke behøves hvis I er påpasselige med hvem 
der kan se videoen. Ifølge straffeloven så er det kun nødvendigt at sløre hvis det skal 
deles i det offentlige rum. 
●
Indirekte identificering er ikke vigtigt. Politiet vil simpelthen ikke bruge ressourcer på 
den slags. 
●
En anden måde at komme over problemerne på er jo simpelt at indhente samtykker.  
●
Igen artikel 9 stk 2 litra j siger at hvis det er til videnskabelige forhold så behøver I 
ikke at sløre. 
==PAGE:159==
15/03/2019 
●
Generelt prøv at holde jer til dataminimerings princippet. Tænk over hvad for noget 
data I gør tilgængeligt og for hvem og vær klar til at forklare hvorfor det er sådan, 
men også vær klar til at fjerne det igen hvis nogen kommer med andre bedre 
argumenter.  
●
Og det vigtigste er at respektere folks rettigheder og privatliv. Det hører alt sammen 
ind under det med transparency i GDPR. Jeg vil på det dybeste anbefale at en 
professionel kigger jeres informationskilde igennem når sådan en er lavet.  
 
 
==PAGE:160==
11/03/2019 
GDPR 2.0 oplæg ​v. Michael Lentge Andersen og Tue Goldschmieding 
 
●
GDPR betyder at nu skal virksomhederne til at tage ansvar 
●
En hacker bruger 6-10 forsøg og så er han inde 
●
IT sikkerhed er et virksomheds problem, ikke et IT problem 
●
Data Breach er også sletning af data 
●
Kompromittering != Data Breach 
●
Ved brud har man 72 timer til at indberette medmindre risikoen er lav. GDPR er 
skrevet af jusiter, så alt er vagt formuleret 
●
Ved brug af kryptering er der lav risiko 
●
Fra 25/5 til 31/12 2018 var der 2780 anmeldte databrud hvoraf de fleste er dumme 
fejl såsom at have sendt en mail forkert  
●
Der er en rød/gul/grøn tilgang til hvem/hvilke sager der bliver anmeldt.  
○
Fordi der er mange indberetninger, er der pt en kumulativ tilgang til hvem der 
bliver anmeldt. Hvis 1 firma har mange indberetninger, så er der faresignaler 
●
Bøder i DK går fra 25.000-15.000.000 kr 
●
Før kunne man tale om tingene, men nu falder hammeren. Ved overtrædelse bliver 
sagen politianmeldt 
○
Der er pt ikke overdraget nogle sager til politiet fra datatilsynet

Structural challenges
Attack capabilities increase
–
Any pattern based security can be circumvented
–
Advanced hackers will at any time defeat machine based solutions
–
AI based on patterns, is still pattern based
–
Detecting and cleaning up after advanced attacks, require more 
network insight than just analysing logs
Structural challenges are considerable
–
Lack of resources in organisations and society in general to detect 
and fight back
–
Increased dependency on equipment suppliers
Hacking is increasingly used by governments and companies
–
Governments and state sponsored hacker groups, increasingly 
attack companies and public organisations for commercial & 
political gain

companies in the United 
States. There are those 
who've been hacked by the 
Chinese, and those who 
don't know they've been 
hacked by the Chinese.“
James Comey, FBI Director, 
October 5, 2014

The cost of not knowing and not being prepared
CASE: TalkTalk, Telecoms operator
October 21, 2015, Hacked
–
Fear: All 4 million customers had their personal data hacked
–
In the news: ”Millions of her customers could have had their data - including 
bank details – stolen”
November 15, 2015
–
Only 157.000 customers had their personal details accessed, i.e. 4% of customers
–
Hereof 15.600 bank account numbers and sort codes, i.e. 0,4% of customers
The aftermath
–
TalkTalk continuously warned their customers against fake calls from criminals 
trying to get them to reveal their information
–
Many customers wanted to shift, but TalkTalk wouldn’t allow them unless they 
would ”be able to show they had lost money as a result of the hack”
–
The attack cost up to £35m in one-off costs
–
Long-term implications on stock value not known
”They didn’t know, and 
that’s what they are 
paying for”
”They were probably 
compliant and living up 
to industry standards”

Breach learnings from the first year with GDPR
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
A breach of data can be due to insufficient security 
precautions or that information is handled in a authorised 
way.
What does GDPR say?
What is a data breach in  
practice?
How is data breach 
assessed?
GDPR’s definition of a ‘personal data breach’ (article 
4): 
‘Personal data breach means a breach of security 
leading to the accidental or unlawful destruction, loss, 
alteration, unauthorised disclosure of, or access to, 
personal data transmitted, stored or otherwise 
processed’. 
Breach learnings from the first year with GDPR
Persons in the data controllers’s own organization 
gain unauthorized access to personal information, 
e.g. an email sent to a wrong recipient, an IT system 
which can be reached by everyone as a consequence 
of lack of access restriction, or because an employee 
leaves documents in the printer or the copy 
machine.
The system manager changes or erases personal 
information by a mistake. It can be an employee 
who mistakenly erases all information in a data 
base that can not be re-established. 
Data is leaked or unintentionally published.
Data is mistakenly sent to a recipient outside the 
organisation.
The following should always concluded in the 
estimation of a data breach:
The character of the breach: has information 
been lost or has the confidence of the 
correctness of the information been 
compromised?
The nature and the extent of the information.
Risk of the data subject to be identified. 
Possible consequences for the data subject: 
potential financial consequences, identity 
theft/fraud, damage to reputation, loss of 
confidence, discrimination or other 
considerable financial or social inconvenience?
Kind of data subjects: subjects being at 
particular risk or children?
Extent of breach: The number of data subjects 
being affected by the breach. 
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
The Danish Data Protection 
Agency
Breach learnings from the first year with GDPR
The Data Subject
As a principal rule all data breaches must be 
reported to the Danish Data Protection Agency.
If the data controller can demonstrate that it is 
unlikely that the breach on the security of the 
personal information involves a risk for the 
data subjects in question, notice can be 
omitted.
It can be the case when it is without doubt that 
there are no unauthorized persons who has 
seen or been capable of copying the information 
before the breach was stopped.
Report must be made without any unnecessary 
delay and, when possible, at the latest 72 hours 
after the system manager has been acquainted 
with the breach. 
Report must be made via the electronic blanket 
available at the Danish Data Protection 
Agency’s website. 
The data controller must inform the data 
subjects in question without any unnecessary 
delay when the system manager estimates that 
the breach of the security of the personal 
information in all probability involves a high risk 
for the data subjects in question. 
The assessment of whether there is a high risk 
must be based on the potential consequences the 
breach can have for the specific data subject. The 
worse consequences the breach can have the 
higher is the risk. 
The notification must describe the character of 
the breach of the security of the personal 
information, the likely consequences as well as 
the measurements the system manager has taken 
or has recommended for the data subject to take 
in order to minimize the damaging effects of the 
breach.
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Extract from the Danish Data Protection Agency’s report on notified 
data breaches for 2018
-
The Danish Data Protection Agency has from 25 May 2018 to 31 December 2018 received 2.780 reports of breach 
of the protection of personal data. Moreover, the Danish Data Protection Agency has received a non-specified 
number of inquiries via  the European data protection advice collaboration portal regarding breach of cross-
border protection of personal data. 
-
The Danish Data Protection Agency: ”It is only very few of the reports which has not involved a breach of the 
protection of personal data, and it must therefore be stated that in general matters are not reported if they are not 
obliged”. 
-
”Another widespread group of reports is information which by mistake has not been subject to  the confidentiality 
which the data controller has deemed necessary for the  handling, e.g. if mails according to internal instructions 
should be send encrypted  are send without being encrypted.”. 
-
80% of the reports concerns less than five registered involved.

The tasks set out in the GDPR
Art. 57
The Article sets out tasks throughout art. 57 (1) (a-v) which the supervisory 
authority shall conduct on its territory. 
(a) monitor and enforce the application of the GDPR;  
(h) conduct investigations on the application of the GDPR […]
Breach learnings from the first year with GDPR
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
The Danish Data Protection Act
Article 29: 
1)
The Data Protection Agency may demand being given all information 
of importance for its activities, including for the decision of whether a 
particular matter falls within the provisions of the General Data 
Protection Regulation and this Act. 
2)
The members and staff of the Data Protection Agency shall at any 
time against appropriate proof of identity and without any court 
warrant have access to all premises from where a personal data 
processing operation is carried out. If required, the police must 
provide assistance with securing such access. 
Breach learnings from the first year with GDPR
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
The Danish Data Protection Act
Article 29: 
1)
This means that the Agency has the right to access:
a)
All rooms of locations where a personal data 
processing operation is carried out, and 
b)
All equipment used to process personal data. 
2)
The Agency can require all information necessary to 
conduct the investigatory tasks of the Agency.

GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Questions
• Overview of systems used for processing personal data?
• Deletion deadline for the particular type of personal data processed?
• How does the system support the deletion deadline?
• Which procedures are implemented to ensure automatic as well as manual deletion?
Deletion Inspection
• Is it required to have a DPO? 
• Based on which grounds?
• If required, is a qualified DPO been designated?
• Has it been notified to the Agency?
DPO Inspection
• Which data processing activities are being performed?
• Which types of personal data is processed and on which legal basis?
• Legal consent?
• Which type of data subjects?
• Is there other factors to consider for the legal basis – the state of the data subjects (children etc.)?
Inspection of Legal 
basis for processing 
personal data
Inspections in practice  
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
The Agency’s take away from the Inspections
–
Be prepared to prove that you are compliant (article 5 (2) and article 24)
–
Its not enough to have a privacy policy – it has to be complied with in practice
–
Know your systems
–
Know which personal data is processed by which system
–
Set a retention period and prepare to prove that there is actual deletion at the end of that period 
– technical as well as manually 
–
There must be a procedure to follow up on enforcement of retention and deletion

Update on fines throughout EU
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Cases regarding fines under the GDPR
−Google imposed a fine of 50 Mio EUR by the French DPA (21 January 2019)
−Violation of the rights of the data subject (vital information on what data is processed, for 
what purposes etc. not transparent)
−No legal basis for using personal data for ads personalization (obtained consent not 
sufficiently informed, specific and unambiguous)
−The size of the fine was justified by the severity of the infringements and the popularity and 
spread of Google’s many services 
−A Portugesian hospitel fined 400,000 EUR by the Portugesian DPA for violation of security 
provisions by giving a large number of employees unauthorized access to highly sensitive data on 
patients (18 June 2018)
Update on fines throughout EU
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Cases regarding fines under the GDPR
−A dating site fined 20,000 EUR by the German DPA (November 2018) for violation of the 
security provision by storing access information in cleartext and without encryption, making it 
possible for hackers to steal more than 300,000 users’ data
−The Norwegian DPA has heralded (December 2018) a fine of 1,6 Mio NOK to a municipality for 
violation of the security provisions by making access data of 35,000 school children  and 
teachers freely available on the internet
Update on fines throughout EU

−Schrems challenging the Privacy Shield Agreement, including the use of standard contracts in 
transfers of personal data to third countries
Fashion ID (C-40/17)
−Does websites with an embedded Facebook ”like” plug-in share a joint data controller 
responsibility with Facebook? The Advocate General (December 2018): Yes! 
−See also Wirtschaftsakademie (Case C-210/16, CJEU decision of 5 June 2018): A social media 
(e.g. Facebook) and the administrator of a fanside on the social media are joint data controllers

GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
How to approach
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
What do we want to obtain?
–
Obtain
–
Correct and well-documented reports of breaches
–
Direct support and estimations of matter of disputes
–
Increased response time
–
The possibility of discovering compromises and breaches before they are notified from outside
–
Safety by knowing that the risk of (undiscovered) compromises is minimal
–
Current overview of network and network activities
–
Save
–
(Extra) audits of the Danish Data Protection Agency because of imprecise, faulty or unnecessary serious reporting (because 
of  data access)
–
Internally and externally overtime work by clarifying extent and data from unknown sources within 72 hours
–
Expensive (panic-driven) incident responses by compromises and breaches which self could be found
–
Avoid
–
Insecurity regarding reporting
–
Unnecessary reporting and imprecise reporting
–
Minimize the risk of financial claims and influence on fire
–
Minimize the risk for downtime
How to approach
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Phase 1: Realising that you (may) have been compromised
Situation A
-
You encounter irregularities that 
may indicate a breach
-
Your internal organisation 
identifies a breach (best case)
Situation B
-
You are informed by authorities or a supplier, 
that you have been compromised
-
Your customers inform you that they have 
been compromised and that the attack has 
been performed via your infrastructure
-
It is exposed publicly that you are 
compromised (worst case)
Two very different situations:
Situation can be contained until it is 
clarified:
- Is it a breach? What is the extent? What are the 
potential consequences? What are our 
obligations? etc.
Situation can’t be contained
- You may be forced to act externally before the 
extent is known
- Limited time and flexibility to clarify situation 
before acting externally
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Handling a compromise: Two key factors decide your available 
response time and flexibility
Detection of a compromise 
or data breach
Preparation for valid incident 
response data
Your ability to discover 
yourself vs. being 
informed from the 
outside
Your ability to qualify if 
there is a data breach 
and the extent of it
How to prepare and manage a data breach - An integrated approach

Phase 1: Realising that you (may) have been compromised
1
2
3
Situation A
-
You encounter irregularities that may 
indicate a breach
-
Your internal organisation identifies a 
breach (best case)
Situation B
-
You are informed by authorities or a supplier, 
that you have been compromised
-
Your customers inform you that they have been 
compromised and that the attack has been 
performed via your infrastructure
-
It is exposed publicly that you are compromised 
(worst case)
Two very different situations:
Situation can be contained until it is 
clarified:
- Is it a breach? What is the extent? What are 
the potential consequences? What are our 
obligations? etc.
Situation can’t be contained
- You may be forced to act externally before the 
extent is known
- Limited time and flexibility to clarify situation 
before acting externally

Who should be informed
Do we need to inform anyone of the breach?
–
Contractual obligations to inform
–
General obligation to act in a loyal manner 
–
Are we acting as data processor?
–
Data breach notification requirements under 
the GDPR
–
Authorities – 72 hours
–
Data subjects – without undue delay if 
there is a high risk
Would it be wise to inform?
–
Obligation to limit damage
–
Gross negligence
–
Confidentiality and penalties
–
Policies and procedures
–
Police report – required for insurance purposes?
Provide information
•Providing information will enable affected 
third parties to limit their losses
•Regulatory or contractual obligations may 
require that we provide information – the 
more information provided the less is the 
risk that we are in breach of these 
obligations
•Not notifying affected third parties (in a 
timely manner) may constitute gross 
negligence 
Limit information
•If we provide information too early there is 
a risk that we will notify unaffected third 
parties or provide incorrect information 
leading to third parties incurring 
unnecessary costs and expenses
•If the number of data subjects is large 
enough the cost of notifying and managing 
requests will be material

What happens:
-
Assessing the extent and 
nature of the breach will in 
most cases require a technical 
compromise assessment
-
In order to scope the technical 
assessment and manage the 
legal aspects of the breach, the 
technical assessment will have 
to be performed in parallel 
and in alignment with the 
legal assessment 
What are the issues:
-
Are third parties involved and 
is there a basis for claims 
against the third parties?
-
When investigating the 
breach, additional issues will 
often arise
-
While this may not be 
intentional, the assessment 
may identify breach of policies 
and procedures by employees
How to control:
-
Establish a joint technical and 
legal assessment scope
-

involved third parties and 
potential claim profile in 
respect of each third party
-
Keep focus and anticipate that 
additional issues may have to 
be prioritised
-
Align with HR on how to 
manage employee related 
aspects of the breach

GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Third parties
Security and 
data protection 
obligations
• What obligations relevant to the breach have the supplier or other third party in question undertaken?
• What derived obligations apply – e.g. obligations of data processors under the GDPR?
Legal basis
• Is there a legal basis for a claim – e.g. non-performance of security obligations or is the attack of such nature that it has 
occurred despite the supplier fulfilling its obligations?
Rights and 
remedies
• What are the rights and remedies available?
• What rights do we have to perform audits and require information in order to perform risk assessments?
Liability
• What limitations of liability apply?
• Have relevant heads of loss been exempted?
• Have hacking, malware etc. been qualified as force majeure?

GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Summary – being in control as DPO
Prepare
Knowledge:
Monitor and Control
Respond
-
Acknowledge that you may be 
compromised
-
Know what to do when, before you 
are compromised
-
Make the hard decisions up front 
– not when the damage is done
-
Make sure to have the right data 
and controls in place to identify a 
breach – before you are told by 
customers or authorities
-
Ensure that contractual 
commitments made from 
suppliers  or from you towards 
customers are supported by you 
internal controls
-
The objective of being prepared is 
limiting the time and efforts 
required to assess and respond to 
a breach while limiting the risk 
exposure to the organisation
-
Being prepared to respond to a 
breach is a good business case
Only if you are prepared, have knowledge and are able to respond you can:
•
Control the process 
•
Decide the right moment to inform
•
Avoid publicity
•
Contain the breach
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Summary – How to continuously prepare as a DPO
–
Take responsibility for a preparedness setup is in place
–
Check for compromise, regularly or continuously, or at least record data breach forensics data
–
Prepare what you can prepare, e.g.
–
How are we obligated to inform of a breach according to our contracts? Are we clear enough 
in our contracts going forward?
–
Employee issues: How and how much can we check employees’ use of internet, mail etc. in 
case of a compromise?
–
How do we act if there has been a security flaw in equipment from a supplier that has led to 
the compromise? Are we covered going forward?
–
What if we have supplied some equipment with security flaws in? What is our position?
GDPR 2.0 Legal-technical handling of major data breaches
March 2019
Summary – Governance ownership of a DPO
–
Take ownership  for the organisation to follow the five good governance principles:
–
Risk driven security & preparedness
–
Separate IT security & info security from IT operations
–
Split the security supply chain in design, supply and check
–
Take ownership for and ensure integrity of the Check-process
–
Prepare according to threat types
–
Respond according to breach type

==PAGE:175==
Interview: Hauler I
I.1
Hauler #1
The ﬁrst hauler interview was conducted in Herning at the transport exhibition with
Kim Ancker. The interview was casually conducted while waiting for exhibition
guests to come to the stand where Ancker had the most secure truck in Denmark
for show. This was also the truck where AUGIT had set up their prototype for the
exhibition. As such, Ancker was familiar with the project. The original interview
notes were written on a mobile phone and afterwards (immediately after) re-written
on the computer.
The interview was in Danish, so a short summary is provided for the English reader:
Ancker thinks it is a good idea to have recordings in a truck as it can be useful in both
insurance cases and potentially for employee appraisals. Furthermore, he accepts
the notion of providing the video for research but is hesitating as both the question
of privacy is a concern but also if it would have an aﬀect worth the eﬀort. In relation
to the platform, then Ancker wants a simple and easy solution that does not take
up unnecessary time.
I.2
Hauler #2
The second hauler interview was conducted in Kastrup at the company K Sand
Andersen Transport with the hauler Kim Sand Andersen.
This interview was
likewise conducted in Danish and a summary is presented: Andersen is a general
supporter of advancement in traﬃc and has several trucks equipped with some form
of prototype to either help the drivers or other road users. He would welcome the
platform and the recording of video and states that he already tracks his drivers
through their location and that the trucks have cameras. (In retrospect, at the time
of the interview it was perceived as the drivers had cameras ﬁlming them, however,
as it was never elaborated it could be that they ’just’ have DashCams). The main
incentive for Andersen is to use the video as evidence but also for research.
163
==PAGE:176==
21/03/2019 
Vognmand ​v. Kim Ancker 
Hvad er dine tanker om at videreudvikle på brillen så den kan optage hvad man ser? 
●
Selvom vi har mange kameraer i lastbilen, så har vi ingen der optager. Jeg har tænkt 
over det før, men det er et virvar at dele video med forsikringsselskabet og jeg kan 
ikke se hvad jeg ellers sådan skulle bruge det til. Bare det med at finde de kabler der 
skal bruges til at uploade filmen fra kameraet til computeren får mig til at give op. Så 
hvis man skulle have noget der optog så skulle det være let at komme til. 
●
I forhold til det personlige så tror jeg at det kunne gavne på det lange sigt. Og vi har 
ikke noget at skjule. Mange folk har en idé om at vi sidder og laver alt mulig andet 
mens vi kører og jeg skal da heller ikke udelukke at nogen laver noget de ikke burde. 
Det er dem der er skyld i den her fordom der gør at ‘den store får skylden’ hvis der 
skulle ske noget. Men ved os, der har vi styr på sagerne så tænker ikke at det ville 
have den store betydning om der kom en lille film ud af det 
 
Hvis der nu var f.eks. en hjemmeside hvor videoen automatisk blev lagt ind, kunne du 
så tænke dig at bruge det? 
●
Ja for pokker. Hvis der ikke er noget bøvl med det så virker det da som en super idé. 
Jeg skal jo alligevel på computeren hver dag. 
 
Når videoen er tilgængelig, hvad kunne den så ellers bruges til? 
●
Forsikring er jo ideelt 
●
Medarbejdersamtaler, men der er nok noget med privatliv der skal værnes om. Hvis 
chaufføren er med på det, så kunne video være et godt udgangspunkt.  
●
Måske kunne de andre trafikanter få et indblik i vores situation fra førerhuset. Det er 
jo aldrig med vilje når vi rammer noget. ​(chauffør kommentar fra siden) 
 
Hvad hvis videoen også kunne deles med f.eks. forskere som kunne bruge det til at 
forbedre forholdene på vejene eller finde generel mangler? 
●
Jeg vil se det før jeg tror det. Sådan noget video tager jo lang tid at finkæmme. Hvis 
de vil vide hvordan vejene er, så ringer de bare. Spøg til side, jeg synes det lyder 
oplagt hvis det kan hjælpe, selvfølgelig, men jeg er også nødt til at tænke på de 
mennesker der er på videoen. Jeg kunne da godt forestille mig at der var ting hist og 
her som ikke skulle på kamera. Jeg ville da selv have lov til at pille bussemænd i fred 
når det nu endelig skal være. Man kan jo selvfølgelig få begge dele hvis der bare er 
mulighed for at jeg kan hoppe ind og slette de videoer der er lidt for afslørende.  
 
Hvordan har du det generelt med teknik? 
●
Der er jeg okay med når det kommer til computeren. Jeg kan også sagtens det med 
kameraet, jeg gider bare ikke når der kommer ekstra ting. Jeg foretrækker det helt 
simpelt og ligetil så man kan forstå det. Hvis det skal slettes, jamen så skriv ‘slet’ i 
stedet for en dum skraldespand og hvis det skal deles så bare klik på det der skal 
deles og skriv hvem det skal deles med. Det er da derfor facebook er så populær. 
Det er simpelt, og ja de har godt nok figurer, men om ikke andet så står der hvad de 
betyder når man holder musen over dem, så man lærer det hurtigt. 
==PAGE:177==
21/03/2019 
 
Hvad ville være brugbart at kunne få af information sammen med videoen? 
●
Den der kører, det er vel lidt selvsagt hvis man skal bruge det til noget 
●
Hvis der er en co med på turen er også en god information 
●
Hvilken lastbil det er har jeg brug for i forhold til hvis det er forsikring i hvert fald 
●
Hvor lang en tur har været. Jeg forestiller mig at der kommer til at være flere videoer 
på en tur, medmindre i optager en 14 timers video med hviletider, hvilket nok ikke er 
særlig nyttigt og nok heller ikke noget folk ville bryde sig om. Men den generelle 
længde på hele turen kunne være nyttig til samtaler, så har jeg det et sted, men altså 
det er jo selvfølgelig i tacho’en så det kan findes. 
 
 
 
==PAGE:178==
03/04/2019 
Vognmand ​v. Kim Sand Andersen 
Hvad beskæftiger I jer med? 
●
Alt, vi har køl, fryse, varme, radioaktiv, vogne til stortset alt hvor vi primært kører 
internt her på Sjælland 
●
Jeg har 24 ansatte hvor kun 3 har været ansat i mindre end 5 år, 18 trailere og 27 
køretøjer lige fra kassevogne til halvstore lastbiler til træk 
●
Vi går meget op I at alt skal være godt også udseendet, derfor vaskes bilerne 
minimum 2 gange om måneden 
 
Hvad indsamler du at data omkring dine ansatte og køretøjer? 
●
Jeg indsamler ingen data, men overvåget køretøjerne ved bl.a. lokation of kamera. 
Så er der dagsedlen som chaufføren kommer hjem med og de holder selv øje med 
køretøjerne og siger hvis der er fejl og mangler sådan sidedele, styretøj eller lift. Det 
taster jeg jo så ind i mit excel ark. 
●
Alle køretøjer har elektronisk tachograph som bliver aflæst hver 20. dag. Det skal 
gemmes i minimum 1 år, men vi gør det i 5. Det er jo bl.a. her der holdes styr på om 
chaufføren holder sine 15 + 30 minutters hvil 
 
Hvordan fungerer det med køre hvile tid? 
●
Det er noget tachografen hjælper til med. Den er en lille sladrehank hvis chaufføren 
ikke holder sine pauser og til tider og lidt for streng. Hvis en chauffør holder 14 
minutters pause og derefter sætter i gang igen, så gælder pausen ikke. Der SKAL 
holder 15.  
 
Hvad bruges tachografen til? 
●
Tacho’en er personlig til chaufføren og tages med videre fra bil til bil. Det er et lille 
kort (viser kortet). Bilen blinker hvis kortet ikke er sat i. 
●
Det smarte system kan skabe problemer ved at køretiden fra 1 firma kan ‘ødelægges’ 
hvis chaufføren også kører for et andet, men sådan er det jo.  
●
Man skal have 3 kort for at køre lastbil i dag, som skal fornyes hvert andet år 
 
Har I haft nogle skader på jeres biler? 
●
Skader, ja det har vi da, men vi er bestemt ikke hårdt ramt. Vi har haft Codan ude og 
holder kurser, men vi har haft enkelte spejle og små skader hist og her, f.eks at en 
trailer kommer for tæt på en rampe.  
●
Vi går op i minimering og snakker sammen om besværlige steder og hjælper 
hinanden og så tager vi på kursus ved bl.a. codan 
 
Hvad gør I for at mindske ulykker med personer? 
●
Vi har haft mange projekter. Lige pt så har vi gummi på siden af traileren der når ned 
til jorden. Det virker lidt ligesom en kost der skubber personer ud af hvis det skulle 
blive ramt, så de ikke ryger ind under lastbilen. 
●
Det er hårdt sagt, men nogen gange er det cyklisternes egen skyld. De har kørt deres 
hjerner fast på at skulle hjem og ser kun lige ud 
==PAGE:179==
03/04/2019 
Hvad ville du sige til hvis AUGIT brillen optog hvad den så? 
●
Det lyder da fornuftigt. Vi bruger jo allerede kameraer i vores biler. Kunderne kan 
godt lide den service det er at kunne forklare hvor deres varer er henne af i landet, 
det er godt nok mest GPS, men vi har også kameraer, så det er ikke meget nyt for os 
med at optage. 
●
Det er nyt at optage hvad chaufføren ser. Det tror jeg godt at vi kunne bruge nogen 
gange. Man hører da irriterende historier, men dem har vi ikke så mange af. 
 
Hvis der fandtes en hjemmeside hvor du kunne dele videoen med dit 
forsikringsselskab, ville du så benytte dig af den? 
●
Det kan jeg da ikke forestille mig at nogen ville sige nej til. Hvis videoen fandtes skal 
man da bruge den. Vi går meget op i at hjælpe hinanden, og jeg har da før været 
vidne til en ulykke hvor jeg gerne ville have hjulpet. Det kunne videoen da.  
●
Vi prøver også gang på gang at få vores naboer over og bruge vores spejl bane så 
de også er sikre i trafikken.  
 
Hvad kunne du forestille dig at det kunne bruges til? 
●
Til at hjælpe hinanden, selvom vi ikke alle arbejder for samme firma så er vi jo stadig 
en slags kolleger med fælles mål. (der hentydes til forsikring)  
●
Som I jo kan se på vores biler, så de stort set alle en eller anden form for prototype 
på fra diverse projekter og jeg kunne da måske forestille mig at codan kunne bruge 
det til deres kurser eller det kunne bruges til forskning 
 
Hvordan har du det med teknik? 
●
Hvis I tænker på computere så helt fint, det bruger jeg jo til dagligt, det bliver alle 
vognmænd nødt til. Nogen har godt nok forskellige programmer til at tage sig af 
deres ting. Det er f.eks. Darko der bliver kørt fra Padborg og Man, Scania og Volvo 
har deres eget hvor det bliver gemt på en eller anden computer. Jeg foretrækker at 
alt gøres her på firmaet.  
 
Hvad ville være brugbar information for dig at have sammen med videoen? 
●
Hvor mange chauffører der er 
●
Detaljer omkring videoen og her mener jeg dato, tid, længde 
●
Hvem chaufførerne er
